Key Takeaway
Abu Zayd al-Marwazi was a towering Shafi'i scholar and a key transmitter of Sahih al-Bukhari through al-Firabri.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Zayd combined deep knowledge, asceticism, and travel for Allah's sake. You have access to books and online courses without leaving home. What excuse do you have for not seeking knowledge with the same sincerity? Will you not set aside even one hour today to learn something of the deen deeply?
?
He was described as the most ascetic (azhaduhum) in this world. Examine your attachment to worldly comforts. Are you willing to give up one luxury this week to draw closer to Allah? What is that one thing you know you should let go of?
?
He traveled multiple times for knowledge, even for Hajj and Jihad. When was the last time you stepped out of your comfort zone for the sake of Allah? In the next month, what step will you take to seek knowledge or do good that requires real effort?

Abu Zayd's Dream: Divine Assistance in Travel
Dream narrative of Abu Zayd with the Prophet and Jibril.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of this dream narrative in highlighting the Prophet's care and the concept of barakah through dreams.

Core Idea
Dreams can be a means of divine aid, as seen when the Prophet sent Jibril with Abu Zayd.

This lesson presents a remarkable dream experienced by the scholar Abu Zayd al-Marwazi. Fearing a long journey, he saw the Prophet and Jibril, and was granted ease. This story illustrates the high spiritual station of Abu Zayd and the reality of true dreams (ru'ya sadiqa).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the two testimonies: first about Abu Zayd's sinlessness, then the dream itself.
The passage begins with Abu Bakr al-Bazzar's testimony.
2
Identify the two testimonies
The passage contains two separate narrations: one praising Abu Zayd's piety, and the other being his own dream account. Mark where one ends and the other begins.
The second testimony starts with 'وعزمت على الرجوع'.
3
Reflect on the dream's content
Focus on the dream: the Prophet sitting, the young man (Jibril), and the Prophet's command. Ask yourself what this reveals about the Prophet's concern for his followers.
The Prophet addresses Jibril as 'ياروح الله' (O Spirit of Allah).
4
Consider the lesson for believers
Think about how this story encourages trusting Allah in difficult situations. The dream removed Abu Zayd's anxiety and hardship. What does this teach about reliance on Allah?
This is not a source of law but a personal experience of divine favor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو عبد الله سمعت أبا بكر البزار يقول عادلت الفقيه أبا زيد من نیسابور إلى مكة فما اعلم ان الملائكة كتبت عليه خطيئة قال وسمعت أبا الحسن محمد بن أحمد الفقيه يعنى ابن عبدوس بن حاتم الحاتمي النيسابورى يقول سمعت أبا زيد الفقيه المروزى يقول لما عزمت على الرجوع إلى خراسان من مكة تقسم قلبي بذلك وكنت اقول متى يمكنني هذا والمسافة بعيدة والمشقة لا أحتملها فقد طعنت في السن فرأيت في المنام كأن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قاعد في صحن المسجد الحرام وعن يمينه شاب فقلت يا رسول الله قد عزمت على الرجوع إلى خراسان والمسافة بعيدة فالتفت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى الشاب بجنبه فقال ياروح الله تصحبه إلى وطنه قال أبو زيد فأريت انه جبريل عليه السلام فانصرفت إلى مرو فلم أحس بشيء من مشقة السفر. هذا ونحوه فإني لم ارجع إلى المكتوب عندى من لفظ أبي الحسن
Abu Abdullah said: I heard Abu Bakr al-Bazzar say: I travelled with the faqih Abu Zayd from Naysabur to Mecca, and I do not know that the angels recorded a sin against him. He said: And I heard Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Faqih — meaning Ibn Abdus ibn Hatim al-Hatimi al-Naysaburi — say: I heard Abu Zayd al-Faqih al-Marwazi say: When I resolved to return to Khurasan from Mecca, my heart was divided about that, and I was saying: When can I do this? The distance is far and I cannot bear the difficulty, for I have become old. So I saw in a dream as if the Messenger of Allah (may peace be upon him) was sitting in the courtyard of the Sacred Mosque, and on his right was a young man. I said: O Messenger of Allah, I have resolved to return to Khurasan, and the distance is far. So the Messenger of Allah turned to the young man beside him and said: O Spirit of Allah, accompany him to his homeland. Abu Zayd said: I was shown that it was Jibril (peace be upon him). So I departed to Marw and did not feel any hardship of travel. This and similar [accounts]; I did not return to what is written with me from the wording of Abu al-Hasan.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage contains two testimonies: first, Abu Bakr al-Bazzar testifies to Abu Zayd's sinlessness during their travel. Second, Abu Zayd himself narrates a dream in which he saw the Prophet in the Haram with a young man on his right. When he expressed his anxiety about the long journey to Khurasan, the Prophet instructed the young man, identified as Jibril (the Spirit of Allah), to accompany him. Abu Zayd then traveled without any hardship. The author (Ibn Asakir) adds that he did not refer to his written record from the wording of Abu al-Hasan, implying the narration is from memory.

Key Terms
أبو زيد المروزي
جبريل
الرؤيا
حسن الظن بالله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dreams like this can be used as sources of Islamic law or theology.
Correction: This dream is a personal experience (ru'ya) and not a source of legislation or doctrine. It illustrates divine favor but does not establish legal rulings.

Checkpoint

B) A young man who was Jibril

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's care for his followers extends even to dreams, providing comfort and aid in times of need.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ cares about your personal struggles, even in your sleep? Have you ever taken a difficult journey or task to the Prophet in your heart and asked for his intercession? If not, why? What would change if you actually did?

?
The ease Abu Zayd felt after the dream was complete. Is there a struggle in your life you have not surrendered to the Prophet's guidance? What is holding you back from asking for his help with full conviction? Commit to a specific action this week.

Abu Zayd al-Marwazi: Life and Legacy
Biographical details including teachers, narrators, and year of death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly contributions of Abu Zayd al-Marwazi, including his teachers, students, and his role in transmitting Sahih al-Bukhari.

Core Idea
Abu Zayd al-Marwazi was a key transmitter of Sahih al-Bukhari and a leading Shafi'i jurist.

This passage provides a detailed biographical sketch of Abu Zayd al-Marwazi, highlighting his status as a hadith scholar and jurist. It traces his teachers, his narration of Sahih al-Bukhari from al-Firabri, and his death in 371 AH. Understanding his legacy helps appreciate the transmission of key Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the biographical details come through.
Pay attention to the chain of narration at the beginning.
2
Identify the chain of narration
The passage begins with a chain of narrators transmitting the biography. Note the names: Abu al-Qasim, Abu al-Hasan, Abu Mansur, Abu Bakr al-Hafiz, then Muhammad Ahmad etc.
This chain indicates the reliability of the report.
3
List Abu Zayd's teachers and students
The passage mentions several teachers (e.g., Muhammad ibn Abdallah al-Sa'di, al-Munkadiri) and students (al-Daraqutni, al-Qaffal al-Marwazi). Make a mental note of them.
His students include prominent hadith scholars.
4
Understand his significance as a transmitter of Sahih al-Bukhari
The passage emphasizes that Abu Zayd was the most eminent narrator of Sahih al-Bukhari from al-Firabri. Recognize the importance of this transmission chain.
This connects to the wider hadith tradition.
5
Note his death year and scholarly legacy
The passage gives his death in Rajab 371 AH. Reflect on how his students, like al-Qaffal, continued his legacy.
This helps place him chronologically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشريف أبو القسم على بن إبراهيم الحسيني وأبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور بن قبيس الفقيه وأبو منصور محمد بن عبدالملك بن حسين بن خيرون قالوا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على الحافظ محمد أحمد بن عبد الله بن عبدالله بن محمد أبو زيد المروزى الفقيه سمع محمد بن عبدالله السعدى وجماعة من اصحاب على بن حجر واكثر عن أبي بكر أحمد بن محمد بن عمر المنكدرى وكان احد أئمة المسلمين حافظا لمذهب الشافعي حسن النظر مشهورا بالزهد والورع ورد بغداد وحدث بها فسمع منه وروى عنه أبو الحسن الدارقطني ومحمد بن أحمد بن القسم المحاملي وخرج أبو زيد إلى مكة فجاور بها وحدث هناك بكتاب صحيح البخاري عن محمد بن يوسف الفربرى وأبو زيد اجل من روى ذلك الكتاب وقال لنا الشيخ أبو القاسم اسماعيل بن أحمد بن السمرقندي قال لنا الشيخ أبو اسحق الشيرازي : أبو زيد محمد بن أحمد عبد الله بن محمد المروزی صاحب بن أبي إسحق مات بمرو في رجب سنة احدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة وكان حافظا للمذهب حسن النظر مشهورا بالزهد وعنه اخذ أبو بكر القفال المروزي وفقهاء مرو .
The sharif Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn Ibrahim al-Husayni, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur ibn Qubays al-Faqih, and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Husayn ibn Khayrun informed us, they said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hafiz said to us: Muhammad Ahmad ibn Abd Allah ibn Abd Allah ibn Muhammad Abu Zayd al-Marwazi al-Faqih heard from Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Sa'di and a group of the companions of Ali ibn Hajar, and he narrated extensively from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Umar al-Munkadiri. He was one of the imams of the Muslims, a hafiz of the Shafi'i school, good in reasoning, famous for asceticism and piety. He came to Baghdad and narrated there, and al-Hasan al-Daraqutni and Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Qasim al-Mahamili heard from him and narrated from him. Abu Zayd went to Mecca and stayed there as a neighbor, and narrated there the book of Sahih al-Bukhari from Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Firabri. And Abu Zayd was the most eminent of those who narrated that book. And Sheikh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi said to us, Sheikh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi said to us: Abu Zayd Muhammad ibn Ahmad Abd Allah ibn Muhammad al-Marwazi, the companion of Ibn Abi Ishaq, died in Marw in Rajab of the year 371 AH. He was a hafiz of the school, good in reasoning, famous for asceticism. From him took Abu Bakr al-Qaffal al-Marwazi and the jurists of Marw.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage provides another chain of transmission for Abu Zayd's biography. It lists his teachers: Muhammad ibn Abdallah al-Sa'di, companions of Ali ibn Hajar, and al-Munkadiri. It reiterates his status as a hafiz of Shafi'i school, his asceticism, his visit to Baghdad where al-Daraqutni and al-Mahamili narrated from him. It emphasizes that he was the most eminent narrator of Sahih al-Bukhari. Finally, it gives his death in Rajab 371 AH in Marw, and notes that Abu Bakr al-Qaffal al-Marwazi and the jurists of Marw were his students.

صحيح البخاري

الفربرى

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'صاحب بن أبي إسحق' is thought to mean 'owner of the son of Abu Ishaq', but it likely means 'the companion of the son of Abu Ishaq', referring to a scholarly relationship.
Correction: The phrase indicates Abu Zayd was a companion or student of the son of Abu Ishaq, a known figure, not a possessive ownership.

The Biography of Abu Zaid al-Marwazi: A Scholar's Dream and Legacy
Ibn Asakir narrates the biography and dream story of Abu Zaid al-Marwazi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly legacy of Abu Zaid al-Marwazi, including the dream story that highlights his spiritual rank.

Core Idea
A dream of the Prophet confirmed Abu Zaid's sanctity and his high status as a scholar.

This lesson presents the biography of Abu Zaid al-Marwazi as recorded by Ibn Asakir. The passage includes a remarkable dream in which the Prophet commands Jibril to accompany Abu Zaid on a difficult journey, demonstrating his spiritual favor. It then details his teachers, his role in transmitting Sahih al-Bukhari, and his legacy among Shafi'i scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the dream story and the subsequent biographical details.
The passage is a blend of narrative and biographical data.
2
Understand the dream story's significance
Consider why this dream is included in a biography. It serves to authenticate Abu Zaid's spiritual status and divine favor, as the Prophet personally commands Jibril to assist him.
Dream stories are common in traditional biographies to highlight a scholar's virtue.
3
Recognize Abu Zaid's scholarly contributions
Note his teachers, his transmission of Sahih al-Bukhari, and his students. This establishes his place in the chain of Islamic learning.
He is described as a 'hafiz' of the Shafi'i school and a model of asceticism.

زید، قال أبو عبد الله سمعت أبا بكر البزار يقول عادلت الفقيه أبا زید من نیسابور إلى مكة فما اعلم ان الملائكة كتبت عليه خطيئة قال وسمعت أبا الحسن محمد بن أحمد الفقيه يعنى ابن عبدوس بن حاتم الحاتمي النيسابورى يقول سمعت أبا زید الفقيه المروزى يقول لما عزمت على الرجوع إلى خراسان من مكة تقسم قلبي بذلك وكنت اقول متى يمكنني هذا والمسافة بعيدة والمشقة لا أحتملها فقد طعنت في السن فرأيت في المنام كأن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قاعد في صحن المسجد الحرام وعن يمينه شاب فقلت يا رسول الله قد عزمت على الرجوع إلى خراسان والمسافة بعيدة فالتفت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى الشاب بجنبه فقال ياروح الله تصحبه إلى وطنه قال أبو زید فأريت انه جبريل عليه السلام فانصرفت إلى مرو فلم أحس بشيء من مشقة السفر. هذا ونحوه فإني لم ارجع إلى المكتوب عندى من لفظ أبي الحسن، أخبرنا الشريف أبو القسم على بن إبراهيم الحسيني وأبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور بن قبيس الفقيه وأبو منصور محمد بن عبدالملك بن حسين بن خيرون قالوا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على الحافظ محمد أحمد بن عبد الله بن عبدالله بن محمد أبو زید المروزى الفقيه سمع محمد بن عبدالله السعدى وجماعة من اصحاب على بن حجر واكثر عن أبي بكر أحمد بن محمد بن عمر المنكدرى وكان احد أئمة المسلمين حافظا لمذهب الشافعي حسن النظر مشهورا بالزهد والورع ورد بغداد وحدث بها فسمع منه وروى عنه أبو الحسن الدارقطني ومحمد بن أحمد بن القسم المحاملي وخرج أبو زید إلى مكة فجاور بها وحدث هناك بكتاب صحيح البخاري عن محمد بن يوسف الفربرى وأبو زید اجل من روى ذلك الكتاب وقال لنا الشيخ أبو القسم اسماعيل بن أحمد بن السمرقندي قال لنا الشيخ أبو اسحق الشيرازي : أبو زید محمد بن أحمد عبد الله بن محمد المروزی صاحب بن أبي اسحق مات بمرو في رجب سنة احدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة وكان حافظا للمذهب حسن النظر مشهورا بالزهد وعنه اخذ أبو بكر القفال المروزي وفقهاء مرو .
Zaid said: Abu Abdullah said: I heard Abu Bakr al-Bazzar say: I accompanied the faqih Abu Zaid from Nishapur to Mecca, and I do not know that the angels recorded a sin upon him. He said: And I heard Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Ahmad the faqih – meaning Ibn Abdus ibn Hatim al-Hatimi al-Naysaburi – say: I heard Abu Zaid the faqih al-Marwazi say: When I resolved to return to Khurasan from Mecca, my heart was divided by that, and I would say: When can I do this? The distance is far and the hardship I cannot bear, for I have become advanced in age. Then I saw in a dream as if the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was sitting in the courtyard of the Sacred Mosque, and on his right was a young man. I said: O Messenger of Allah, I have resolved to return to Khurasan and the distance is far. The Messenger of Allah turned to the young man beside him and said: O Spirit of Allah, accompany him to his homeland. Abu Zaid said: So I was shown that he was Jibril, peace be upon him. Then I departed to Marw and did not feel any hardship of travel. This and similar – for I did not refer back to what was written with me from the wording of Abu al-Hasan. Al-Sharif Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn Ibrahim al-Husayni and Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur ibn Qubays al-Faqih and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Husayn ibn Khayrun informed us, they said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hafiz Muhammad Ahmad ibn Abdullah ibn Abdullah ibn Muhammad Abu Zaid al-Marwazi al-Faqih said to us: He heard Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Sa'di and a group of the companions of Ali ibn Hajar, and mostly from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Umar al-Munkadiri. He was one of the imams of the Muslims, a memorizer of the Shafi'i school, excellent in opinion, famous for asceticism and piety. He visited Baghdad and narrated there, and he was heard from. Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni and Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Qasim al-Mahamili narrated from him. Abu Zaid went out to Mecca and resided there, and narrated there the book of Sahih al-Bukhari from Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Farabri. Abu Zaid is the greatest of those who narrated that book. And Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi said to us, Shaykh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi said to us: Abu Zaid Muhammad ibn Ahmad Abdullah ibn Muhammad al-Marwazi, the companion of Ibn Abi Ishaq, died in Marw in Rajab of the year 371 AH. He was a memorizer of the school, excellent in opinion, famous for asceticism. From him Abu Bakr al-Qaffal al-Marwazi and the fuqaha of Marw took knowledge.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Zaid al-Marwazi, transmitted through multiple chains of narration. It begins with a dream story in which the Prophet Muhammad (s) commands Jibril (the Spirit of Allah) to accompany Abu Zaid on his journey from Mecca to Khurasan, removing all hardship. Then the text provides his full name and teachers, including Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Sa'di and Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Munkadiri. It emphasizes his status as a leading Shafi'i jurist, his asceticism, and his narration of Sahih al-Bukhari from al-Farabri. The entry concludes with his death date and notes that he was the source of knowledge for many scholars, including Abu Bakr al-Qaffal al-Marwazi.

الفربرى

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dream is merely a personal anecdote without theological significance.
Correction: In this context, the dream authenticates Abu Zaid's spiritual rank and divine favor, as it is recorded by multiple chains and shows the Prophet's direct intervention.

The Scholarly and Spiritual Station of Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif
Ibn Asakir's biographical entry on Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the high status of Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif as both a Shafi'i jurist and a Sufi master, and the importance of combining exoteric and esoteric knowledge.

Core Idea
True Sufism is built on profound knowledge of the Shariah.

In this biography, Ibn Asakir introduces us to a towering figure who mastered both the outward sciences of Islam and the inward path. Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif was not only a Sufi but also a faqih (jurist) of the Shafi'i school. His life exemplifies the integration of legal scholarship and spiritual discipline.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography entry
Read the Arabic text and translation. Notice the chain of transmission and the details of his lineage and teachers.
Ibn Khafif was from Shiraz, his mother from Nishapur.
2
Identify his qualities
Find the phrases that describe his knowledge, his adherence to the Book and Sunnah, and his role as a faqih.
He is described as 'اعلم المشايخ بعلوم الظاهر' (most knowledgeable in exoteric sciences).
3
Understand his view on Sufism
Read the quote about Sufism ending with him and his response to the one who spoke with lofty speech. What does this teach about genuine Sufism?
Sufism that comes cheaply is sold cheaply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو عبد الله بن خفيف الشيرازي الصوفي رحمته الله ) أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن اسماعيل الفارسي في كتابه قال انا أبو بكر محمد بن يحيى بن إبراهيم المزكى قال انا أبو عبدالرحمن الحسين السلمي قال : محمد بن خفیف بن اسفكشاذ الضبي أبو محمد بن عبد الله المقيم بشيراز كانت امه نيسابورية هو اليوم شيخ المشايخ وتاريخ الزمان لم يبق للقوم اقدم منه سنا ولا اتم حالا ووقتا صحب رويما والجريري وأبا العباس بن عطاء ولقى الحسين بن منصور وهو من اعلم المشايخ بعلوم الظاهر متمسكا بعلوم الشريعة من الكتاب والسنة وهو فقيه على مذهب الشافعى وقال أحمد بن يحيى الشيرازى ما ارى التصوف إلا ويختم بأبي عبدالله بن خفيف وقيل لأبي عبدالله بن خفيف ان فلانا تكلم في التصوف بكلام عال فقال انه قام عليه التصوف رخيصا فهو يبيعه رخيصا، نعى الينا سنة احدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة كتب إلى الشيخ أبو على الحسن بن أحمد ابن الحسن المقري قال انا أبو نعيم أحمد بن عبد الله بن أحمد الحافظ قال ومنهم أبو عبد الله محمد ابن خفيف الظريف له الفصول في الأصول والتحقق والتثبت في الوصول لقى الأكابر والإعلام صحب رويما وأبا العباس بن عطاء وطاهرا المقدسي وأبا عمر الدمشقي كان شيخ الوقت حالا وعلما توفى سنة احدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة، أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم زاهر ابن طاهر بن محمد المستملي قال انا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقي قال سمعت أبا الحسن علی بن حمزة بن على العلوى يقول سمعت أبا عبدالله محمد بن عبدالله الشيرازي يقول نظر أبو عبد الله بن خفيف يوما الى ابن مكتوم وجماعة من اصحابه يكتبون شيئا فقال ما هذا فقالوا نكتب كذا وكذا فقال اشتغلوا بتعلم شيء ولا يغرنكم كلام الصوفية فإني كنت أخبىء محبرتي في جيب مرقعتى والكاغد في حجرة سراويلي وكنت اذهب خفية إلى أهل العلم فإذا علموا بي خاصموني وقالوا لا تفلح ثم احتاجوا إلى بعد ذلك، سمعت الشيخ أبا بكر محمد بن أحمد بن الحسن البروجردي ببغداد يقول سمعت أبا سعد على بن عبدالله بن أبي صادق الحيرى بنيسابور يقول سمعت أبا عبدالله محمد بن عبدالله بن باكويه
And among them is Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif al-Shirazi al-Sufi, may Allah have mercy on him. (Chain) Al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il al-Farisi informed us in his book, he said: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Ibrahim al-Muzakki informed us, he said: Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Husayn al-Sulami informed us, he said: Muhammad ibn Khafif ibn Asfkashad al-Dabbi, Abu Muhammad ibn Abdullah, resident in Shiraz, his mother was from Nishapur. He is today the shaykh of the shaykhs and the unique of the time; there remains among the people no one older in age nor more complete in state and time. He accompanied Ruwaym, al-Jurayri, and Abu al-Abbas ibn Ata, and met al-Husayn ibn Mansur. He is among the most knowledgeable of the shaykhs in the exoteric sciences, adhering to the sciences of the Shariah from the Book and the Sunnah, and he is a faqih according to the Shafi'i school. Ahmad ibn Yahya al-Shirazi said: I do not see Sufism except that it ends with Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif. It was said to Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif: So-and-so spoke about Sufism with lofty speech. He said: Sufism came to him cheaply, so he sells it cheaply. He died – news reached us in the year 371 AH. (Another chain) He wrote to al-Shaykh Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Muqri, he said: Abu Nu'aym Ahmad ibn Abdullah ibn Ahmad al-Hafiz informed us, he said: And among them is Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Khafif al-Zarif; he has al-Fusul fi al-Usul (Chapters on Fundamentals) and al-Tahqiq wa al-Tathabbat fi al-Wusul (Verification and Confirmation in Attainment). He met the great ones and the prominent figures; he accompanied Ruwaym, Abu al-Abbas ibn Ata, Tahir al-Maqdisi, and Abu Umar al-Dimashqi. He was the shaykh of the time in state and knowledge. He died in the year 371 AH. Al-Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir ibn Muhammad al-Mustamli informed us, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi informed us, he said: I heard Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Hamza ibn Ali al-Alawi say: I heard Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Shirazi say: Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif looked one day at Ibn Maktum and a group of his companions writing something. He said: What is this? They said: We are writing such-and-such. He said: Occupy yourselves with learning something, and do not let the talk of the Sufis deceive you. For I used to hide my inkwell in the pocket of my patched cloak and the paper in the waistband of my trousers, and I would go secretly to the people of knowledge. When they found out about me, they would oppose me and say: You will not succeed. Then later they needed me.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif al-Shirazi, a prominent Sufi and Shafi'i jurist. It begins with a chain of transmission and describes his lineage, his teachers (Ruwaym, al-Jurayri, Ibn Ata), and his meeting with al-Hallaj. It highlights his mastery of both exoteric sciences (fiqh, Qur'an, Sunnah) and esoteric knowledge. A saying from Ahmad ibn Yahya al-Shirazi asserts that Sufism culminates with Ibn Khafif. The entry includes a critique of those who speak loftily about Sufism without substance. Two death notices confirm he died in 371 AH. The passage ends with an anecdote where Ibn Khafif advises his students to focus on learning substantive knowledge rather than being deceived by mere Sufi talk, recounting how he himself had to hide his writing materials to study in secret, and later those who opposed him needed him.

Key Terms
أبو عبد الله بن خفيف
رویم
الجریري
ابن عطاء
التصوف

Key Terms from Source Passage

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Secret Learning of Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif
Anecdote from Ibn Khafif's life

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn from the early dedication of Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif to seeking knowledge in secret despite opposition, and his advice to his companions to focus on substantive learning.

Core Idea
Seek knowledge with sincerity, even if you have to hide it.

This anecdote from Ibn Khafif's life reveals a powerful lesson for students of knowledge. When he saw his companions writing something, he did not discourage writing but warned against being deceived by mere Sufi talk without solid learning. He then shared his own experience of hiding his inkwell and paper to study secretly, because the people of knowledge initially opposed him. Eventually, those same people came to need him.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the Arabic story from the chain. Understand the setting: Ibn Khafif sees his companions writing and asks what they are writing.
The companions were writing something, perhaps Sufi sayings.
2
Analyze his response
He told them to occupy themselves with learning something and not to be deceived by Sufi talk. Why do you think he said that?
He valued substantive knowledge over empty spiritual talk.
3
Reflect on his personal story
He describes how he used to go secretly to scholars, hiding his tools. What does this teach about the importance of seeking knowledge?
He persevered despite opposition and later became a reference.

ومنهم أبو عبد الله بن خفيف الشيرازي الصوفي رحمته الله ) أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن اسماعيل الفارسي في كتابه قال انا أبو بكر محمد بن يحيى بن إبراهيم المزكى قال انا أبو عبدالرحمن الحسين السلمي قال : محمد بن خفیف بن اسفكشاذ الضبي أبو محمد بن عبد الله المقيم بشيراز كانت امه نيسابورية هو اليوم شيخ المشايخ وتاريخ الزمان لم يبق للقوم اقدم منه سنا ولا اتم حالا ووقتا صحب رويما والجريري وأبا العباس بن عطاء ولقى الحسين بن منصور وهو من اعلم المشايخ بعلوم الظاهر متمسكا بعلوم الشريعة من الكتاب والسنة وهو فقيه على مذهب الشافعى وقال أحمد بن يحيى الشيرازى ما ارى التصوف إلا ويختم بأبي عبدالله بن خفيف وقيل لأبي عبدالله بن خفيف ان فلانا تكلم في التصوف بكلام عال فقال انه قام عليه التصوف رخيصا فهو يبيعه رخيصا، نعى الينا سنة احدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة كتب إلى الشيخ أبو على الحسن بن أحمد ابن الحسن المقري قال انا أبو نعيم أحمد بن عبد الله بن أحمد الحافظ قال ومنهم أبو عبد الله محمد ابن خفيف الظريف له الفصول في الأصول والتحقق والتثبت في الوصول لقى الأكابر والإعلام صحب رويما وأبا العباس بن عطاء وطاهرا المقدسي وأبا عمر الدمشقي كان شيخ الوقت حالا وعلما توفى سنة احدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة، أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم زاهر ابن طاهر بن محمد المستملي قال انا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقي قال سمعت أبا الحسن علی بن حمزة بن على العلوى يقول سمعت أبا عبدالله محمد بن عبدالله الشيرازي يقول نظر أبو عبد الله بن خفيف يوما الى ابن مكتوم وجماعة من اصحابه يكتبون شيئا فقال ما هذا فقالوا نكتب كذا وكذا فقال اشتغلوا بتعلم شيء ولا يغرنكم كلام الصوفية فإني كنت أخبىء محبرتي في جيب مرقعتى والكاغد في حجرة سراويلي وكنت اذهب خفية إلى أهل العلم فإذا علموا بي خاصموني وقالوا لا تفلح ثم احتاجوا إلى بعد ذلك، سمعت الشيخ أبا بكر محمد بن أحمد بن الحسن البروجردي ببغداد يقول سمعت أبا سعد على بن عبدالله بن أبي صادق الحيرى بنيسابور يقول سمعت أبا عبدالله محمد بن عبدالله بن باكويه
And among them is Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif al-Shirazi al-Sufi, may Allah have mercy on him. (Chain) Al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il al-Farisi informed us in his book, he said: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Ibrahim al-Muzakki informed us, he said: Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Husayn al-Sulami informed us, he said: Muhammad ibn Khafif ibn Asfkashad al-Dabbi, Abu Muhammad ibn Abdullah, resident in Shiraz, his mother was from Nishapur. He is today the shaykh of the shaykhs and the unique of the time; there remains among the people no one older in age nor more complete in state and time. He accompanied Ruwaym, al-Jurayri, and Abu al-Abbas ibn Ata, and met al-Husayn ibn Mansur. He is among the most knowledgeable of the shaykhs in the exoteric sciences, adhering to the sciences of the Shariah from the Book and the Sunnah, and he is a faqih according to the Shafi'i school. Ahmad ibn Yahya al-Shirazi said: I do not see Sufism except that it ends with Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif. It was said to Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif: So-and-so spoke about Sufism with lofty speech. He said: Sufism came to him cheaply, so he sells it cheaply. He died – news reached us in the year 371 AH. (Another chain) He wrote to al-Shaykh Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Muqri, he said: Abu Nu'aym Ahmad ibn Abdullah ibn Ahmad al-Hafiz informed us, he said: And among them is Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Khafif al-Zarif; he has al-Fusul fi al-Usul (Chapters on Fundamentals) and al-Tahqiq wa al-Tathabbat fi al-Wusul (Verification and Confirmation in Attainment). He met the great ones and the prominent figures; he accompanied Ruwaym, Abu al-Abbas ibn Ata, Tahir al-Maqdisi, and Abu Umar al-Dimashqi. He was the shaykh of the time in state and knowledge. He died in the year 371 AH. Al-Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir ibn Muhammad al-Mustamli informed us, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi informed us, he said: I heard Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Hamza ibn Ali al-Alawi say: I heard Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Shirazi say: Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif looked one day at Ibn Maktum and a group of his companions writing something. He said: What is this? They said: We are writing such-and-such. He said: Occupy yourselves with learning something, and do not let the talk of the Sufis deceive you. For I used to hide my inkwell in the pocket of my patched cloak and the paper in the waistband of my trousers, and I would go secretly to the people of knowledge. When they found out about me, they would oppose me and say: You will not succeed. Then later they needed me.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif al-Shirazi, a prominent Sufi and Shafi'i jurist. It begins with a chain of transmission and describes his lineage, his teachers (Ruwaym, al-Jurayri, Ibn Ata), and his meeting with al-Hallaj. It highlights his mastery of both exoteric sciences (fiqh, Qur'an, Sunnah) and esoteric knowledge. A saying from Ahmad ibn Yahya al-Shirazi asserts that Sufism culminates with Ibn Khafif. The entry includes a critique of those who speak loftily about Sufism without substance. Two death notices confirm he died in 371 AH. The passage ends with an anecdote where Ibn Khafif advises his students to focus on learning substantive knowledge rather than being deceived by mere Sufi talk, recounting how he himself had to hide his writing materials to study in secret, and later those who opposed him needed him.

Key Terms
أبو عبد الله بن خفيف
التصوف
محبرة
مرقعة

Key Takeaway
True knowledge requires dedication and patience; Ibn Khafif's example shows the value of seeking knowledge even in difficult circumstances.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
Anecdotes of Ibn Khafif's Asceticism and Devotion
Ibn Asakir narrates multiple anecdotes about the asceticism and piety of Abu Abd Allah Ibn Khafif.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the extreme asceticism and strict adherence to the Sunna of Abu Abd Allah ibn Khafif are illustrated through specific anecdotes.

Core Idea
Asceticism without abandon – Ibn Khafif's discipline was rooted in the Sunna.

The passage from Ibn Asakir presents a series of firsthand accounts that paint a vivid portrait of a true ascetic. These stories show not only his renunciation of worldly comforts but also his meticulous following of the Prophetic example. Let's examine each anecdote to uncover the depths of his devotion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the complete Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the multiple chains of transmission and the vivid details in each story.
The passage uses multiple 'I heard' chains, typical of hadith and biographical works.
2
Identify the themes in each anecdote
Go through each anecdote and note what aspect of Ibn Khafif's character it highlights: extreme asceticism, strict sunna compliance, humility, charity, or discipline.
3
Reflect on the integration of zuhd and sunna
Consider how Ibn Khafif's asceticism is not a rejection of the Sunna but its embodiment. His actions are based on prophetic reports, like the hadith on sitting prayer and the emphasis on sunan in ablution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشيرازي يقول سمعت أبا عبد الله بن خفيف يقول كنت في ابتدائي بقيت أربعين شهرا أفطر كل ليلة بكف باقلاء فمضيت يوما وافتصدت فخرج من عرقي شبيه ماء اللحم وغشى على فتحير الفصاد وقال : ما رأيت جسدا بلا دم إلا هذا، قال وسمعت أبا عبد الله يقول : ما سمعت شيئا من سنن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلا استعملته حتى الصلاة على أطراف الأصابع، سمعت الشيخ أبا المظفر عبد المنعم بن عبد الكريم بن هوازن القشيري يقول سمعت أبي الأستاذ أبا القسم يقول سمعت أبا عبد الله بن باكويه الشيرازي يقول سمعت أبا العباس الكرجي يقول سمعت أبا عبد الله بن خفيف يقول ضعفت عن القيام في النوافل وقد جعلت بدل كل ركعة من أورادي ركعتين قاعدا للخبر «صلاة القاعد على النصف من القائم» وسمعت أبا المظفر يقول سمعت أبي يقول سمعت الشيخ أبا عبد الله بن باكويه الكوفي الصوفي يقول سمعت أبا عبد الله بن خفيف يقول ما وجبت علي زكاة الفطر أربعين سنة ولي قبول عظيم بين الخاص والعام، سمعت أبا بكر محمد بن أحمد الأسدي الجوهري يقول سمعت علي بن عبد الله النيسابوري يقول سمعت محمد بن عبد الله الصوفي يقول سمعت أبا أحمد الكبير قال كان أبو عبد الله إذا أراد أن يخرج إلى صلاة الجمعة يقول لي : هات ما عندنا فأحمل إليه كل ما قد فتح من الذهب والفضة وغيره فيفرقه كله ثم يخرج إلى صلاة الجمعة، وكان كل سنة لا يبقى لنفسه ما يخرج به [؟] أوانه يخرج جميـ إلى براو ما عنده من الثياب حتى [؟] من صلاة [؟] أخبرنا أبو بكر الجوهري قال أنا أبو سعيد الحيري قال أنا أبو عبد الله بن باكويه قال ثنا أبو أحمد الصغير قال كان أمرني يعني ابن خفيف أن أقدم إليه كل ليلة عشر حبات زبيب لإفطاره قال فأشفقت عليه ليلة فجعلتها ست عشرة فنظر إلي وقال من أمرك بهذا وأكل منها عشر حبات وترك الباقي.
Al-Shirazi said: I heard Abu Abd Allah ibn Khafif say: In my beginning I remained forty months, breaking my fast every night with a handful of broad beans. Then one day I went and was bled, and from my vein came out something resembling meat-water, and I fainted; the phlebotomist was astonished and said: I have never seen a body without blood except this one. He said: And I heard Abu Abd Allah say: I never heard anything of the Sunnas of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, except that I practiced it, even the wiping on the tips of the fingers. I heard the Shaykh Abu al-Muzaffar Abd al-Mun’im ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin al-Qushayri say: I heard my father, the Ustadh Abu al-Qasim, say: I heard Abu Abd Allah ibn Bakawayh al-Shirazi say: I heard Abu al-Abbas al-Karaji say: I heard Abu Abd Allah ibn Khafif say: I became too weak to stand for voluntary prayers, so I made instead of every rak‘a of my regular devotions two rak‘as sitting, because of the report: “The prayer of one sitting is half of the prayer of one standing.” And I heard Abu al-Muzaffar say: I heard my father say: I heard the Shaykh Abu Abd Allah ibn Bakawayh al-Kufi al-Sufi say: I heard Abu Abd Allah ibn Khafif say: The zakat al-fitr was not obligatory upon me for forty years, and I had great acceptance among the elite and commoners. I heard Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Asadi al-Jawhari say: I heard Ali ibn Abd Allah al-Naysaburi say: I heard Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Sufi say: I heard Abu Ahmad al-Kabir say: Abu Abd Allah, when he wanted to go out to Friday prayer, would say to me: Bring what we have. So I would carry to him all the gold, silver, and other things that had been opened, and he would distribute all of it, then go out to Friday prayer. And every year he would not keep for himself what he would wear [?] then he would go out, entire, to [?] what he had of garments, even [?] of prayer [?]. Abu Bakr al-Jawhari informed us, saying: Abu Sa‘id al-Hayri informed us, saying: Abu Abd Allah ibn Bakawayh informed us, saying: Abu Ahmad al-Saghir narrated to us, saying: He commanded me — meaning Ibn Khafif — that I should bring to him every night ten raisins for his breaking of fast. He said: One night I felt compassion for him and made it sixteen. He looked at me and said: Who commanded you to do this? And he ate ten of them and left the rest.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a collection of biographical anecdotes about the renowned Sufi Abu Abd Allah ibn Khafif, transmitted through multiple chains of narration. Each story highlights a different aspect of his character and practice. The first anecdote illustrates his extreme asceticism: he fasted for forty months, breaking his fast each night with only a handful of broad beans. When he was bled, his blood resembled meat-water and he fainted, astonishing the phlebotomist, who said he had never seen a body without blood except this one. The second story shows his meticulous adherence to the Sunna: whenever he heard of any practice of the Prophet, he would implement it, even to the extent of performing ablution up to the tips of the fingers. The third relates that when he became too weak to stand for voluntary prayers, he replaced each rak‘a of his regular devotions with two rak‘as sitting, citing the hadith that the prayer of one sitting is half that of one standing. The fourth anecdote reveals his humility: he claimed that zakāt al-fiṭr was not obligatory upon him for forty years (implying he possessed no surplus wealth), yet he was highly accepted among both elite and commoners. The fifth story describes his charity before Friday prayer: he would gather all the gold, silver, and goods that had come to him and distribute them entirely before going to prayer. The final anecdote concerns his strict discipline: he instructed his attendant to bring exactly ten raisins for his nightly breaking of fast. When the attendant once increased it to sixteen out of compassion, Ibn Khafif noticed, asked who commanded the increase, ate only ten, and left the remainder. The passage emphasizes his asceticism, strict adherence to the Sunna, humility, and self-discipline.

Key Terms
asceticism (zuhd)
sunna
zakat al-fitr
voluntary prayers (nawafil)
breaking fast (iftar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Ibn Khafif's claim that zakat al-fitr was not obligatory for forty years indicates neglect of an obligation.
Correction: It actually indicates he possessed no surplus wealth (nisab) during that period, so the obligation did not apply.

Checkpoint
What did Ibn Khafif do when his attendant brought him sixteen raisins instead of ten?
A) He ate all sixteen.
B) He scolded the attendant and ate nothing.
C) He ate only ten and asked who commanded the increase.
D) He gave them to the poor.

Key Takeaway
True asceticism is disciplined by the Sunna, not a rejection of it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What sunna of the Prophet have you known for a long time but consistently failed to implement? Will you commit to acting on it starting today, no matter how small?
?
Ibn Khafif maintained strict discipline even in the smallest matters, like eating exactly ten raisins. Where in your life do you allow yourself to exceed limits out of 'compassion' for yourself, when what your soul really needs is discipline? What is one specific boundary you will set this week?
?
He gave away all his wealth before Friday prayer, trusting Allah completely. What possession, comfort, or relationship are you clinging to that holds you back from worshipping Allah with full freedom? Could you take one concrete step to let it go this week as an act of trust?

Biography of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili: A Model of Traditional Scholarship
Ibn Asakir provides a detailed biographical sketch of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the exemplary life and scholarly legacy of Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili: a scholar whose sessions attracted multitudes and earned praise from Daraqutni and Dhahabi.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir presents a detailed biographical sketch of the hadith master Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. Through the transmission of Hamza al-Sahmi, we learn about his birth, death, character, and the vast circles of students who gathered around him. This account not only preserves his scholarly achievements but also offers a window into the vibrant tradition of hadith learning in the fourth Islamic century.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic carefully, then the literal translation to grasp the full narrative.
Notice the isnad (chain of transmission) at the beginning.
2
Identify key biographical details
Note his full name, death date, age, and the mention of his parents.
The blessing of his parents' prayers is highlighted.
3
Observe the scholarly scene
Understand how al-Isma'ili taught and how students from far and wide attended his sessions.
The list of students shows the breadth of his influence.
4
Reflect on the testimonies
Consider the praise from the vizier and al-Daraqutni, and the later remark by al-Dhahabi.
These testimonies elevate his status as a giant among early scholars.
5
Connect to your own learning
Think about what we can learn from his dedication and the transmission of knowledge through such chains.
This biography is a model for seeking knowledge.

ومنهم أبو بكر الجرجاني المعروف بالإسماعيلي رحمه الله. أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم بن أبي بكر الكتبي قال أنا أبو القسم إسماعيل بن مسعدة بن إسماعيل الجرجاني قال أنا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف السهمي الجرجاني في تاريخ جرجان قال: أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن العباس أبو بكر الإسماعيلي، الإمام رحمه الله وبيض وجهه وألحقه بعباده الصالحين توفي يوم السبت غرة رجب سنة إحدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة وكان له أربع وتسعون سنة. سمعت والدي أبا يعقوب يوسف بن إبراهيم بن موسى يقول كان أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم الإسماعيلي بارا بوالديه لحقته بركة دعائهما. قال حمزة وسألني الوزير أبو الفضل جعفر بن الفضل بن الفرات بمصر عن أبي بكر الإسماعيلي وما صنف وجمع وعن سيرته فكنت أخبره بما صنف من الكتب وجمع من المسانيد والمقلين وتخريجه على كتاب محمد بن إسماعيل البخاري، وجميع سيرته فتعجب ذلك وقال لقد كان رزق من العلم والجاه وكان له صيت حسن. وقال حمزة سمعت أبا الحسن الدارقطني الحافظ يقول كنت قد عزمت غير مرة أن أرحل إلى أبي بكر الإسماعيلي فلم أرزق. قال حمزة وكنت إذا حضرت مجلس الإمام أبي بكر الإسماعيلي ورأيته لم يتفوه بشيء من تفسير خبر أو ضرب مثل أو حكاية أو بيت شعر أو نادرة أو غير ذلك من سائر العلوم إلا وتبادر جماعة من الغرباء وأهل البلد علقوا وكتبوا خصوصا أبو بكر البرقاني فإنه قلما كان يترك شيئا يجري إلا وهو يكتب وكذلك أبو القسم الورثاني وأبو جعفر محمد بن علي بن دلان الجرجاني، والفضل بن أبي سعد الهدوي وأبو الفضل المخزومي البصري وأبو سعد الماليني وأبو القسم عيسى بن عباد الدينوري ويحيى الأبهري وأحمد بن عبد الرحمن الشيرازي وأبو بكر الجرجاني، وعبد الرحمن السجزي وغيرهم رحمهم الله لا أحصي عددهم وما من يوم إلا وكان بحضرته من الغرباء الجوالين ممن يفهم ويحفظ مقدار أربعين أو خمسين نفسا وكنت أعلق عنه مقدار فهمي وحفظي وأنسخ مما علق عنه أبو بكر البرقاني وأبو جعفر بن دلان الجرجاني. من (١) منها (مسند عمر) هذبه في مجلدين قال الذهبي: طالعته وعلقت منه انبهرت بحفظ هذا الإمام وجزمت بأن المتأخرين على إياس من أن يلحقوا المتقدمين في الحفظ والمعرفة.
Among them is Abu Bakr al-Jurjani, known as al-Isma‘ili, may Allah have mercy on him. The Shaykh Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Bakr al-Katibi informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Isma‘il ibn Mas‘ada ibn Isma‘il al-Jurjani informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf al-Sahmi al-Jurjani informed us in the History of Jurjan, saying: Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma‘il ibn al-Abbas, Abu Bakr al-Isma‘ili, the Imam, may Allah have mercy on him and whiten his face and join him to His righteous servants, died on Saturday, the first of Rajab, in the year three hundred and seventy-one, and he was ninety-four years old. I heard my father Abu Ya‘qub Yusuf ibn Ibrahim ibn Musa say: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Isma‘ili was dutiful to his parents, and the blessing of their supplication reached him. Hamza said: The vizier Abu al-Fadl Ja‘far ibn al-Fadl ibn al-Furat in Egypt asked me about Abu Bakr al-Isma‘ili, what he authored and compiled, and about his biography, so I would inform him about what books he authored, what Musnads and collections he compiled, and his abridgment of the book of Muhammad ibn Isma‘il al-Bukhari, and all his biography; he marveled at that and said: He was surely given knowledge and prestige, and he had a good reputation. And Hamza said: I heard Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni, the hadith master, say: I had resolved more than once to travel to Abu Bakr al-Isma‘ili, but I was not granted it. Hamza said: Whenever I attended the session of Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma‘ili and saw that he did not utter anything of explanation of a hadith, or giving an example, or a story, or a line of poetry, or an anecdote, or anything else of the various sciences, except that a group of strangers and locals would hasten to write it down — especially Abu Bakr al-Burqani, who seldom left anything that occurred without writing it; and likewise Abu al-Qasim al-Warathani, Abu Ja‘far Muhammad ibn ‘Ali ibn Dalan al-Jurjani, al-Fadl ibn Abi Sa‘d al-Hadawi, Abu al-Fadl al-Makhzumi al-Basri, Abu Sa‘d al-Malini, Abu al-Qasim ‘Isa ibn ‘Abbad al-Dinawari, Yahya al-Abhari, Ahmad ibn ‘Abd al-Rahman al-Shirazi, Abu Bakr al-Jurjani, ‘Abd al-Rahman al-Sijzi, and others, may Allah have mercy on them — I cannot count their number. And there was no day except that in his presence there were about forty or fifty traveling strangers, those who understand and memorize. I would record from him according to my understanding and memorization, and I would copy from what Abu Bakr al-Burqani and Abu Ja‘far ibn Dalan al-Jurjani recorded from him. (1) Among them is the Musnad of ‘Umar, which he compiled in two volumes. Al-Dhahabi said: I examined it and annotated it; I was amazed at the memory of this Imam and concluded that the later scholars are in despair of ever catching up with the earlier ones in memory and knowledge.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry from the History of Jurjan, transmitted by Hamza al-Sahmi. It begins with the full name and death date of Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma‘il al-Isma‘ili al-Jurjani, noting that he died on Saturday, 1 Rajab 371 AH at the age of 94. His father testifies that he was dutiful to his parents and benefited from the blessing of their prayers. The vizier Ja‘far ibn al-Furat praised his scholarly output and reputation. Al-Daraqutni, the renowned hadith master, expressed regret at not being able to travel to him. The passage then describes his scholarly sessions: he spoke on various sciences — hadith explanation, examples, stories, poetry, anecdotes — and students would eagerly write down his words. A long list of notable students is given, including al-Burqani, al-Warathani, and others. The narrator Hamza himself would record from him and copy from his students. The passage concludes with a footnote (presumably from the editor or a later source) mentioning that among his works is a Musnad of ‘Umar in two volumes, and quoting al-Dhahabi’s admiration for his memory, stating that later scholars are in despair of equaling the early masters.

Correction: His large student circle and praise from al-Daraqutni and al-Dhahabi indicate his high stature.

Biography of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani
Ibn Asakir relates the biography of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, his learning, students, and works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, scholarly achievements, and reverence of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili as a major hadith and fiqh scholar in the Ash'ari tradition.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili combined hadith, fiqh, and leadership, earning admiration from scholars like al-Daraqutni.

Ibn Asakir presents a detailed biography of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, a towering figure in hadith and fiqh. Through multiple chains of narration, we learn about his piety, his vast scholarly output, and the high esteem in which he was held. This lesson explores the key details of his life as recorded by his contemporaries.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the full passage to get an overview of al-Isma'ili's life and the various testimonies about him.
2
Identify the testimonies
Note the different narrators: Hamza al-Sahmi, al-Daraqutni, Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, etc. Each adds a dimension to his character.
Al-Daraqutni's desire to visit shows his fame.
3
Focus on his works
The passage mentions his Sahih (on Bukhari's conditions), musnads, and his commentary. Consider what this says about his expertise.
4
Reflect on his teaching sessions
The description of his assemblies with many students writing down everything highlights his role as an educator.
5
Summarize his legacy
Combine the testimonies to appreciate why he is remembered as a polymath leader.

ومنهم أبو بكر الجرجاني المعروف بالاسماعیلی رحمه أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم بن أبي بكر الكتبي قال انا أبو القسم اسماعيل بن مسعدة بن اسماعيل الجرجاني قال انا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف السهمى الجرجاني في تاريخ جرجان قال : أحمد بن إبراهيم بن اسماعيل بن العباس أبو بكر الاسماعيلي، الامام رحمه الله وبيض وجهه والحقه بعباده الصالحين توفى يوم السبت غرة رجب سنة احدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة وكان له اربع وتسعون سنة سمعت والدى أبا يعقوب يوسف ابن إبراهيم بن موسى يقول كان أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم الاسماعيلي بارا بوالديه لحقته بركة دعائهما، قال حمزة وسألني الوزير أبو الفضل جعفر بن الفضل بن الفرات بمصر عن أبي بكر الاسماعيلى وما صنف وجمع وعن سيرته فكنت اخبره بما صنف من الكتب وجمع من المسانيد والمقلين وتخريجه على كتاب محمد بن اسماعيل البخارى، وجميع سيرة فتعجب ذلك وقال لقد كان رزق من العلم والجاه وكان له صيت حسن، وقال حمزة سمعت أبا الحسن الدارقطنى الحافظ يقول كنت قد عزمت غير مرة أن أرحل إلى أبي بكر الاسماعيلى فلم ارزق، قال حمزة وكنت اذا حضرت مجلس الامام أبي بكر الاسماعيلى ورأيته لم يتفوه بشيء من تقسير خبر أو ضرب مثل أو حكاية أو بيت شعر أو نادرة أو غير ذلك من سائر العلوم إلا وتبادر جماعة من الغرباء وأهل البلد علقوا وكتبوا خصوصا أبو بكر البرقاني فإنه قلما كان يترك شيئا يجرى إلا وهو يكتب وكذلك أبو القسم الورثانى وأبو جعفر محمد بن علی بن دلان الجرجاني، والفضل بن أبي سعد الهدوى وأبو الفضل المخزومي البصرى وأبو سعد الماليني وأبو القسم عیسی بن عباد الدينوري ويحيى الابهرى وأحمد بن عبدالرحمن الشيرازي وأبو بكر الجرجاني، وعبدالرحمن السجزى وغيرهم رحمهم الله لا أحصى عددهم وما من يوم إلا وكان بحضرته من الغرباء الجوالين ممن يفهم ويحفظ مقدار اربعين أو خمسين نفسا وكنت اعلق عنه مقدار فهمى وحفظى وأنسخ مما علق عنه أبو بكر البرقاني وأبو جعفر بن دلان الجرجانی، أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم اسماعيل بن أحمد السمرقندي قال ثنا أبو اسحق إبراهيم بن على الفقيه قال : أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم بن اسماعيل بن العباس الاسماعيلي مات سنة نيف وسبعين وثلاثمائة وجمع بين الفقه والحديث ورياسة الدين والدنيا وصنف الصحيح واخذ عنه ابنه أبو سعد وفقهاء جرجان، وقال شيخنا القاضى الامام أبو الطيب الطبري رحمه الله دخلت جرجان قاصدا إليه وهو حى فمات قبل أن ألقاه، جمع بين الأصول والفقه والحديث وصنف صحيحا على شرط البخارى رحمه الله، يدل على فضل كثير لمن وقف عليه أخبرنا الشريف أبو بكر أحمد بن عبدالرحمن ابن أحمد المروزى الواعظ بدمشق قال قال لنا الشيخ الحافظ أبو نصر هبة الله ابن عبد الجبار بن فاخر بن معاذ بن أحمد بن محمد السجزي بسجستان : أبو بكر الاسماعيلى شيخ كبير جليل ثقة من الفقهاء والمحدثين في عصره يرجع إلى علم وافر ومعرفة بالحديث صادقة ومروءة ظاهرة وكانت إليه الرحلة في زمانه وهو أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم بن اسماعيل بن العباس الإسماعيلى الجرجاني روى عن أبي خليفة والمشايخ ولد سنة سبع وسبعين ومائتين ومات سنة احدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة
Among them is Abu Bakr al-Jurjani, known as al-Isma'ili, may Allah have mercy on him. We were informed by the Shaykh Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Bakr al-Katibi, who said: we were told by Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Mas'ada ibn Isma'il al-Jurjani, who said: we were told by Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf al-Sahmi al-Jurjani in the History of Jurjan, who said: Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, the Imam, may Allah have mercy on him, brighten his face, and join him with His righteous servants. He died on Saturday, the first of Rajab, in the year 371 AH, and he was ninety-four years old. I heard my father Abu Ya'qub Yusuf ibn Ibrahim ibn Musa say: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Isma'ili was dutiful to his parents and was blessed by their supplication. Hamza said: The vizier Abu al-Fadl Ja'far ibn al-Fadl ibn al-Furat asked me in Egypt about Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, what he authored, compiled, and his biography. So I informed him of the books he authored, the musnads and the 'less narrators' he compiled, his commentary on the book of Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Bukhari, and all of his biography. He was amazed and said: He was indeed granted knowledge and status, and he had a good reputation. Hamza said: I heard Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni, the hafiz, say: I resolved more than once to travel to Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili but was not enabled. Hamza said: Whenever I attended the assembly of Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili and saw him, he did not utter anything in explanation of a tradition, giving an example, a story, a line of poetry, a rare anecdote, or anything else from the various sciences, but a group of strangers and locals would immediately take notes and write, especially Abu Bakr al-Barqani, who hardly ever left anything spoken without writing it down, as well as Abu al-Qasim al-Warthani, Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn Dilan al-Jurjani, al-Fadl ibn Abi Sa'd al-Hadawi, Abu al-Fadl al-Makhzumi al-Basri, Abu Sa'd al-Malini, Abu al-Qasim 'Isa ibn 'Abbad al-Dinawari, Yahya al-Abhari, Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman al-Shirazi, Abu Bakr al-Jurjani, 'Abd al-Rahman al-Sijizi, and others—may Allah have mercy on them—I cannot count their number. And not a day passed but there were present with him about forty or fifty traveling strangers who understood and memorized. And I would take down notes according to my understanding and memory, and I copied from what Abu Bakr al-Barqani and Abu Ja'far ibn Dilan al-Jurjani had taken down. We were informed by the Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi, who said: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn 'Ali al-Faqih narrated to us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas al-Isma'ili died around 370 AH. He combined fiqh, hadith, and leadership in religion and world, and authored the Sahih. His son Abu Sa'd and the jurists of Jurjan studied under him. Our teacher, the Qadi Imam Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, may Allah have mercy on him, said: I entered Jurjan intending to visit him, but he died before I met him. He combined the principles, fiqh, and hadith, and authored a Sahih according to the conditions of al-Bukhari, may Allah have mercy on him, which indicates great excellence to whoever examines it. The noble Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ahmad al-Marwazi al-Wa'iz informed us in Damascus, saying: The hafiz, the Shaykh Abu Nasr Hibat Allah ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Fakhr ibn Mu'adh ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sijzi told us in Sijistan: Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili is a great, venerable shaykh, trustworthy among the jurists and hadith scholars of his time, possessing abundant knowledge, sincere knowledge of hadith, and manifest manliness. People traveled to him in his time. He is Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani. He narrated from Abu Khalifa and other shaykhs. He was born in the year 277 AH and died in the year 371 AH.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, presented through multiple chains of narration. It begins with a chain from Hamza al-Sahmi, who quotes his father about al-Isma'ili's filial piety and the blessing he received from his parents' supplication. Then Hamza reports the vizier's inquiry about al-Isma'ili's works, noting his compilation of musnads and his commentary on Bukhari. Al-Daraqutni's testimony shows the high regard for al-Isma'ili, as he wished to travel to him. The passage then describes al-Isma'ili's teaching sessions, where many scholars and students would write down everything he said, listing several of his attendees. The following chain from Abu al-Qasim al-Samarqandi emphasizes that al-Isma'ili combined fiqh and hadith and held leadership in both religious and worldly affairs. Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari's comment highlights his scholarship in usul, fiqh, and hadith, and his Sahih on the conditions of Bukhari. Finally, the chain from al-Sijzi gives his birth and death dates and confirms his status as a trustworthy scholar. The biography demonstrates the reverence for this early Ash'ari scholar who was a major figure in hadith and fiqh.

Correction: The text shows he also excelled in fiqh and principles (usul), and held leadership in both religious and worldly affairs.

Biography of Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari
Ibn Asakir introduces Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari as a student and propagator of Ash'ari school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari as a student of Imam al-Ash'ari and his contributions to spreading the Ash'ari school in Syria.

Core Idea
Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari: a devoted student of al-Ash'ari who carried his teachings to Syria.

Ibn Asakir's biographical dictionary introduces us to a key figure in the transmission of Ash'ari theology. Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari was not just a student of al-Ash'ari but an active propagator of his school in Syria. He also authored a foundational work on usul. Let's explore his life and contribution.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical passage
Read the Arabic passage once without translation, then read the literal translation. Notice the key details about al-Tabari's life and teachers.
Pay attention to his kunya 'Abu al-Hasan' which matches his teacher's.
2
Identify his relationship with al-Ash'ari
The passage states he was 'among the notable companions of Abu al-Hasan (al-Ash'ari)' and 'studied under him'. Note that he traveled to Syria to spread the Ash'ari school.
3
Reflect on his scholarly work
He wrote from Abu Ja'far al-Tabari the famous Tafsir. He also authored a book on usul titled 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi wa Basirat al-Mustahdi'. Think about the significance of this title.
The title suggests it was designed to train beginners in theology.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو الحسن عبد العزيز بن محمد بن اسحق الطبري المعروف بالدمل رحمه الله كان من اعيان اصحاب أبى الحسن وممن تخرج به وخرج إلى الشام ونشربها مذهبه وكتب عن أبي جعفر محمد بن جرير الطبري كتابه في التفسير وسمعه منه ووقفت له قديما على تأليف فى الأصول يدل على فضل كثير وعلم غزير سماه كتاب رياضة المبتدى وبصيرة المستهدى
Among them is Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Tabari, known as al-Damal, may Allah have mercy on him. He was among the notable companions of Abu al-Hasan (al-Ash'ari) and among those who studied under him. He traveled to Syria and spread his (al-Ash'ari's) school there. He wrote from Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari his book of Tafsir and heard it from him. I came across an earlier work of his on the principles (usul) that indicates great excellence and abundant knowledge, which he titled 'The Training of the Beginner and the Insight of the Seeker.'
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a brief biographical notice for Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari, known as al-Damal. It states that he was one of the distinguished companions of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and studied under him. He traveled to Syria and propagated the Ash'ari school there. He also wrote from Abu Ja'far al-Tabari (the famous historian and exegete) his Tafsir and listened to it directly from him. The author (Ibn Asakir) mentions that he saw an earlier composition by al-Tabari on usul (principles of jurisprudence or theology) that demonstrated his extensive knowledge, titled 'The Training of the Beginner and the Insight of the Seeker.' This highlights his role in spreading Ash'ari theology and his scholarly output.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Confusing this Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari with the famous historian and exegete Abu Ja'far al-Tabari (author of Tafsir al-Tabari).
Correction: The Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari in this passage is a different person. He was a student of al-Ash'ari and studied under Abu Ja'far al-Tabari, not the same as his teacher.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari: Student of al-Ash'ari and Author on Divine Attributes
Ibn 'Asakir introduces a key student of al-Ash'ari and his famous work on attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly profile of Abu al-Hasan 'Ali al-Tabari, his relationship with al-Ash'ari, and his contribution to interpreting hadiths on God's attributes.

Core Idea
Al-Tabari authored the key Ash'ari work on interpreting problematic attribute hadiths.

This lesson introduces Abu al-Hasan 'Ali al-Tabari, a direct student of Imam al-Ash'ari who became a distinguished scholar and author. His most famous work addresses a critical theological issue: how to understand hadiths that seem to describe God in human-like terms. This passage from Ibn 'Asakir gives us a brief but important glimpse into his life and legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical entry
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the isnad at the end connecting Ibn 'Asakir to his source.
The isnad shows the chain of transmission for this information.
2
Identify al-Tabari's relationship to al-Ash'ari
The passage uses words like 'sahiba' (accompanied), 'akhadha 'anhu' (took from him), and 'takharraja bihi' (graduated under him). Understand the strong student-teacher bond.
3
Focus on his famous book
Al-Tabari wrote a famous book on the interpretation of problematic hadiths about God's attributes. This is a key Ash'ari text dealing with tanzih (transcendence).
The book's title is often given as 'Kitab Ta'wil al-Ahadith al-Mushkilat'.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Be careful not to confuse this al-Tabari with other scholars named al-Tabari, such as the historian or the mufassir. This one is specifically the Ash'ari theologian.
The common misunderstanding is addressed in the misconception section.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو الحسن على بن محمد بن مهدی الطبري صحب أبا الحسن رحمه الله بالبصرة والخذ عنه وتخرج به واقتبس وصنف تصانيف عدة تدل على علم واسع وفضل بارع وهو الذي ألف الكتاب المشهور فى تأويل الأحاديث المشكلات الواردة في الصفات أخبرنا الفقيه ابو الفتح نصر الله بن محمد بن عبدالقوى المصيصي بدمشق
Among them is Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Mahdi al-Tabari. He accompanied Abu al-Hasan (al-Ash'ari), may Allah have mercy on him, in Basra, took from him, graduated under him, and acquired knowledge. He authored several works that indicate extensive knowledge and brilliant excellence. He is the one who wrote the famous book on the interpretation of problematic hadiths related to the attributes. The faqih Abu al-Fath Nasr Allah ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Qawi al-Misisi informed us in Damascus.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a short biographical entry for Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Tabari. It states that he accompanied Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari in Basra, learned from him, and became a distinguished scholar. He authored multiple works demonstrating his vast knowledge. Crucially, he is the author of a famous book that interprets problematic hadiths concerning the divine attributes (sifat), a key topic in Ash'ari theology where anthropomorphic expressions are interpreted metaphorically to preserve God's transcendence. The passage ends with an isnad showing Ibn Asakir's source for this information.

Key Terms
أبو الحسن
الصفات
تأويل الأحاديث المشكلات
البصرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might confuse Abu al-Hasan 'Ali al-Tabari with the famous historian and mufassir Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari (d. 310 AH), or with another scholar named al-Tabari.
Correction: This al-Tabari is a different person: he was a student of al-Ash'ari, lived in Basra, and authored a work on the interpretation of attribute hadiths. He is known as a mutakallim (theologian) of the Ash'ari school, not a historian or universal commentator.

Checkpoint

B) Tafsir
C) The interpretation of problematic hadiths on the attributes of God
D) History

Key Takeaway
Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari was a direct student of al-Ash'ari and wrote the authoritative Ash'ari work on interpreting problematic hadiths about God's attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that al-Tabari accompanied al-Ash'ari and took from him directly. Who is the living scholar you are learning from right now? Are you personally accompanying them—or merely consuming content? What would change if you treated your learning as a relationship, not a transaction?
?
Al-Tabari wrote a famous book interpreting hadiths about Allah's attributes. When you encounter a verse or hadith that seems to describe Allah in human terms, does your mind immediately trust the scholars' interpretation, or do you feel a pull to take it literally? What does your reaction reveal about your heart's purity in tawhid?

The Scholar Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili: A Model of Integrated Knowledge
Ibn Asakir narrates the biography of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili through multiple chains, emphasizing his scholarly breadth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the profile of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili as a Shafi'i jurist, hadith master, and author of a Sahih collection on al-Bukhari's conditions, as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili united jurisprudence, hadith, and leadership.

In this lesson, we explore the biography of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili as transmitted by Ibn Asakir. The passage uses multiple chains to convey his scholarly stature, emphasizing his combination of fiqh and hadith, his authorship of a Sahih, and the high esteem in which he was held. It also corrects the misconception that he was merely a hadith specialist.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage from Ibn Asakir, then its literal translation. Notice the two different chains of transmission (isnads) and how they present complementary information.
2
Identify key biographical details
List the key facts: his full name, birth and death dates, his scholarly contributions (especially the Sahih), and his teachers and students.
Pay attention to the phrase 'جمع بين الفقه والحديث' which sums up his dual expertise.
3
Reflect on the significance of his Sahih
The passage states his Sahih is 'on the conditions of al-Bukhari'. Consider what this implies about his methodology and the value of his work.
This shows he was a leading hadith scholar who followed al-Bukhari's rigorous standards.
4
Examine the misconception
The common misunderstanding is that al-Isma'ili was only a hadith scholar. The text explicitly states he combined fiqh, hadith, and leadership. Note how both chains highlight this.
This lesson guards against reducing his legacy to a single field.

Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn 'Ali al-Faqih narrated to us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas al-Isma'ili died in the year around seventy and three hundred [371 AH]. He combined jurisprudence and hadith and the leadership of religion and the world, and he authored the Sahih. His son Abu Sa'd and the jurists of Jurjan studied with him. Our shaykh, the judge imam Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, may Allah have mercy on him, said: I entered Jurjan intending to visit him while he was alive, but he died before I met him. It indicates great excellence for whoever examines it. He possessed abundant knowledge, sincere knowledge of hadith, and manifest chivalry. People traveled to him in his time. He is Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani. He narrated from Abu Khalifa and the shaykhs. He was born in the year seven and seventy and two hundred [277 AH] and died in the year one and seventy and three hundred [371 AH].
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili (d. 371 AH), a prominent Shafi'i scholar, hadith master, and jurist from Jurjan. The text first provides his death date and highlights that he combined fiqh, hadith, and leadership in both religious and worldly affairs. He authored a Sahih collection, and many scholars, including his son Abu Sa'd and the jurists of Jurjan, studied under him. The judge Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari notes that he traveled to Jurjan to meet him but al-Isma'ili died before the meeting. Another chain adds that al-Isma'ili was a great, reliable shaykh, possessing abundant knowledge and sincere expertise in hadith, and people undertook journeys to him. His birth is given as 277 AH and death as 371 AH.

?

The Chain of Ash'ari Learning: Al-Dumali
Ibn Asakir introduces a student of al-Ash'ari and his usul book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of Abu al-Hasan al-Dumali in transmitting Ash'ari doctrine and the significance of his book 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi' wa Basirat al-Mustahdi'.

Core Idea
Al-Dumali was a key student of al-Ash'ari who spread his school in Syria and wrote an influential usul work.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari introduces us to a lesser-known but important figure: Abu al-Hasan al-Dumali al-Tabari. A direct student of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, he was instrumental in spreading the Ash'ari school in Syria. Ibn Asakir also mentions a manuscript he saw—a book on usul (principles of religion) that reflects deep knowledge. Let's explore this brief biography.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage from Ibn Asakir once, then the English translation. Notice the concise style of biographical entries in classical works.
2
Identify key figures and their roles
Note that al-Dumali is a companion (sahib) of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and also studied tafsir under Abu Ja'far al-Tabari. Distinguish his primary affiliation with al-Ash'ari.
He is not a student of al-Tabari in theology, only in tafsir.
3
Focus on the book title
Examine the title 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi' wa Basirat al-Mustahdi.' Consider what it tells us about the content: it is a guide for beginners and seekers of guidance in usul al-din.
The title suggests pedagogical intent.
4
Reflect on the transmission chain
Think about how knowledge was passed: al-Ash'ari taught al-Dumali, who then traveled to Syria to spread the school. This illustrates the importance of teacher-student networks in Islamic theology.

Source Text

ومنهم أبو الحسن عبد العزيز بن محمد بن اسحق الطبري ) المعروف بالدمل رحمه الله كان من اعيان اصحاب أبى الحسن وممن تخرج به وخرج إلى الشام ونشربها مذهبه وكتب عن أبي جعفر محمد بن جرير الطبري كتابه في التفسير وسمعه منه ووقفت له قديما على تأليف فى الأصول يدل على فضل كثير وعلم غزير سماه كتاب ) رياضة المبتدى وبصيرة المستهدى .
Among them is Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Tabari, known as al-Dumali, may Allah have mercy on him. He was among the notable companions of Abu al-Hasan [al-Ash'ari] and among those who graduated under him. He went out to Syria and spread his [al-Ash'ari's] school there. He wrote from Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari his book of tafsir and heard it from him. I came across an old work of his on principles (usul) that indicates great excellence and abundant knowledge; he named it 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi' wa Basirat al-Mustahdi.'
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari, known as al-Dumali (perhaps derived from 'daml' meaning 'grease' or a place name). He was a prominent companion and student of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and he traveled to Syria to propagate the Ash'ari school. He also studied under Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari, the famous historian and mufassir, and copied or heard his tafsir directly from him. Ibn 'Asakir mentions that he saw a work by al-Dumali on usul al-din (principles of religion) which demonstrated great learning; its title is 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi' wa Basirat al-Mustahdi' (The Training of the Beginner and the Insight of the Seeker of Guidance).

أبو الحسن الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Dumali was primarily a student of Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari in fiqh or theology.
Correction: He studied tafsir from al-Tabari, but his primary affiliation and doctrinal training were under Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Biography of Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari: An Ash'ari Disciple and His Poetry
Ibn Asakir records the biography of Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari, another Ash'ari disciple, including his poetry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly lineage of Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari as a student of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and the content of his poetry reflecting on companionship and the plight of the times.

Core Idea
Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari wrote a key work on hadith attributes and his poetry shows a wise outlook on life.

This lesson introduces another important figure from the Ash'ari school: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari. He was a direct student of al-Ash'ari in Basra and authored a famous book on the interpretation of problematic hadiths about God's attributes. We will also look at two poems he composed, which offer moral and reflective insights.

Guided Path
1

Read the opening lines to see who Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari was and under whom he studied.
His teacher is Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.
2

The book is 'Ta'wil al-Ahadith al-Mushkilat'.
3
Examine the chain of transmission for his poetry
The passage includes a chain of narrators for the poems. Understand the importance of isnad in preserving such material.
The chain goes back through several scholars.

The first poem emphasizes the value of having a good companion. Reflect on its meaning.
It says 'He who has a companion who can improve his affairs is not lost.'
5

The second poem laments the passing of noble people and the futility of regret. Consider its moral lesson.
It contains the phrase 'if only' and 'would that' indicating regret.

Among them is Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Mahdi al-Tabari. Commentary
This passage introduces Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Mahdi al-Tabari, another disciple of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who studied under him in Basra and authored several works. The first poem emphasizes the value of having a good companion who can improve one's state, and that a person is known by his brothers. The second poem laments the passing of noble people and the speaker's remaining in a state of regret ('if only' and 'would that'), with a fragment about generosity that is partially corrupt.

Abu Ja'far al-Naqqash: An Early Ash'ari Theologian
Ibn 'Asakir transmits the biography of Abu Ja'far al-Naqqash, an Ash'ari theologian and hadith scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, scholarly credentials, and theological affiliation of Abu Ja'far al-Naqqash as recorded by Ibn 'Asakir.

Core Idea
A trustworthy Ash'ari theologian who taught kalam to his students.

This biographical passage introduces us to Abu Ja'far al-Naqqash, a scholar of both hadith and kalam. Through the testimony of his contemporaries, we see his reliability as a transmitter and his role in spreading the Ash'ari school. The details of his birth and death help place him in the timeline of Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the full Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, focusing on the names and key phrases. Notice the chain of transmission: Ibn 'Asakir reports from al-Azhari, who reports from al-Naqqash's students.
2
Trace his name and lineage
Identify his full name and epithet 'al-Naqqash', meaning 'the engraver'. Note his lineage back several generations to establish his identity.
His name includes 'al-Sulami' (related to the tribe of Sulaym) and 'al-Baghdadi' (from Baghdad).
3
List his teachers and students
From the passage, identify the scholars he narrated from (teachers) and those who narrated from him (students). This shows his place in the scholarly network.
Teachers include al-Baghawi and Ibn Abi Dawud; students include Abu 'Ali ibn Shadhan and al-Azhari.
4
Understand his theological affiliation
Al-Azhari states that al-Naqqash was a theologian (mutakallim) following the Ash'ari school, and that he taught kalam to Abu 'Ali ibn Shadhan. Note the significance of this for Ash'ari history.
5
Confirm his trustworthiness and dates
Al-Azhari explicitly calls him 'thiqah' (trustworthy). The passage also gives his birth (294 AH) and death (379 AH), placing him in the 3rd-4th centuries AH.
The death date is given as Sunday/Monday, 6 Muharram 379 AH.
